--- MCQ Batch 1 (100 Questions) ---
Topic: Database Fundamentals & Basic SQL (DDL, DML, DQL, DCL, TCL)

1. Question: Which of the following is a major disadvantage of the traditional File System approach compared to a DBMS?
A) High data security
B) Data redundancy and inconsistency
C) Efficient data retrieval
D) Simple data sharing
Correct Answer: B

2. Question: What does the 'R' in RDBMS stand for?
A) Record
B) Retrieval
C) Relational
D) Recursive
Correct Answer: C

3. Question: Which of the following is a characteristic of a traditional file-based system as described in the reference material?
A) Multi-user support
B) Server-client architecture
C) Single-user access
D) Built-in relational capabilities
Correct Answer: C

4. Question: RDBMS design is primarily based on rules developed by Codd at which technology company?
A) Microsoft
B) Oracle
C) IBM
D) Sun Microsystems
Correct Answer: C

5. Question: Which of the following is NOT one of the core CRUD operations supported by all databases?
A) Create
B) Retrieve
C) Index
D) Delete
Correct Answer: C

6. Question: Which category of SQL commands is responsible for managing user permissions and access control?
A) DDL
B) DML
C) DCL
D) TCL
Correct Answer: C

7. Question: The `CREATE TABLE` command falls under which category of SQL?
A) DML
B) DDL
C) DCL
D) TCL
Correct Answer: B

8. Question: Which SQL command is used to add new rows to a table?
A) ADD
B) UPDATE
C) INSERT
D) MERGE
Correct Answer: C

9. Question: The `SELECT` command belongs to which category of SQL?
A) DML
B) DQL
C) DCL
D) TCL
Correct Answer: B

10. Question: Which command is used to permanently remove a table structure and all its data from the database?
A) DELETE
B) REMOVE
C) DROP
D) TRUNCATE
Correct Answer: C

11. Question: Which SQL command is used to change the structure of an existing table, such as adding a new column?
A) MODIFY
B) ALTER
C) RENAME
D) UPDATE
Correct Answer: B

12. Question: Which SQL command is used to change existing data in one or more rows of a table?
A) INSERT
B) MODIFY
C) UPDATE
D) ALTER
Correct Answer: C

13. Question: Which category of SQL commands is used to manage the changes made by DML statements, such as making them permanent?
A) DDL
B) DCL
C) DQL
D) TCL
Correct Answer: D

14. Question: Which TCL command is used to undo all changes since the last COMMIT or SAVEPOINT?
A) UNDO
B) ROLLBACK
C) REVERT
D) SAVEPOINT
Correct Answer: B

15. Question: What is the purpose of the `COMMIT` command in SQL?
A) To save a temporary state of a transaction
B) To make all changes in the current transaction permanent
C) To undo the last DML operation
D) To grant a user permission
Correct Answer: B

16. Question: Which of the following is a valid DCL command?
A) CREATE USER
B) INSERT INTO
C) SELECT FROM
D) ROLLBACK
Correct Answer: A

17. Question: In MySQL, which storage engine was primarily used in versions less than 5.5?
A) InnoDB
B) MyISAM
C) NDB
D) Falcon
Correct Answer: B

18. Question: Which data type is described as having "Fixed inline storage" and "Very fast access"?
A) VARCHAR
B) TEXT
C) CHAR
D) BLOB
Correct Answer: C

19. Question: Which data type is described as having "Variable external storage" and is "Not ideal for indexing"?
A) CHAR
B) VARCHAR
C) TEXT
D) INT
Correct Answer: C

20. Question: When using the `INSERT INTO table SELECT...` syntax, what is the source of the data being inserted?
A) A file on the server
B) Another table in the database
C) A user-defined function
D) A stored procedure
Correct Answer: B

21. Question: What is the special value in SQL that is not stored in the database and cannot be compared using standard relational operators?
A) ZERO
B) EMPTY
C) NULL
D) UNDEFINED
Correct Answer: C

22. Question: Which operator is used to check for the special value mentioned in the previous question?
A) = NULL
B) IS NULL
C) <> NULL
D) NULL CHECK
Correct Answer: B

23. Question: Which logical operator is used in the `WHERE` clause to combine two conditions where both must be true?
A) OR
B) NOT
C) XOR
D) AND
Correct Answer: D

24. Question: The `BETWEEN` operator in the `WHERE` clause is inclusive. What does this mean?
A) It includes the starting value but excludes the ending value.
B) It excludes the starting value but includes the ending value.
C) It includes both the starting and ending values.
D) It excludes both the starting and ending values.
Correct Answer: C

25. Question: In the `LIKE` operator pattern matching, what does the `%` symbol represent?
A) Any single character
B) Any number of any characters
C) Exactly one digit
D) A fixed set of characters
Correct Answer: B

26. Question: In the `LIKE` operator pattern matching, what does the `_` (underscore) symbol represent?
A) Any number of any characters
B) Any single character
C) A space character
D) The end of the string
Correct Answer: B

27. Question: Which clause is used to sort the result set of a `SELECT` query?
A) GROUP BY
B) SORT BY
C) ORDER BY
D) ARRANGE BY
Correct Answer: C

28. Question: By default, the `ORDER BY` clause sorts the results in which order?
A) Descending (DESC)
B) Random
C) Ascending (ASC)
D) Alphabetical
Correct Answer: C

29. Question: To select only the top 10 rows from a table, which clause is typically used in MySQL?
A) TOP 10
B) FETCH FIRST 10 ROWS
C) LIMIT 10
D) HEAD 10
Correct Answer: C

30. Question: What is the purpose of using a column alias in a `SELECT` statement (e.g., `SELECT c1 AS col1`)?
A) To change the column name in the database table
B) To provide a temporary, more readable name for the column in the result set
C) To define a new data type for the column
D) To enforce a unique constraint
Correct Answer: B

31. Question: Which of the following is a system database in MySQL that contains internal/system information?
A) user_data
B) performance_schema
C) client_db
D) application_log
Correct Answer: B

32. Question: What is the purpose of the `DISTINCT` keyword in a `SELECT` statement?
A) To count the number of rows
B) To retrieve only unique values from the specified column(s)
C) To sort the results in a unique order
D) To filter out NULL values
Correct Answer: B

33. Question: In a sharded cluster, which servers store the clusterâ€™s metadata?
A) Local servers
B) Config servers
C) Master servers
D) Query servers
Correct Answer: B

34. Question: What is the minimum number of config servers typically recommended for a production sharded cluster?
A) 1
B) 2
C) 3
D) 4
Correct Answer: C

35. Question: Which type of partitioning ensures an even distribution of data at the expense of efficient range queries?
A) Range-based partitioning
B) Hash-based partitioning
C) Table-based partitioning
D) Document-based partitioning
Correct Answer: B

36. Question: What does SQL stand for?
A) Structured Query Language
B) Standard Question Logic
C) Sequential Query Language
D) System Query Logic
Correct Answer: A

37. Question: Which of the following is a Transaction Control Language (TCL) command?
A) GRANT
B) ALTER
C) SAVEPOINT
D) DELETE
Correct Answer: C

38. Question: What is the maximum length for table and column names in MySQL, as mentioned in the reference?
A) 10 chars
B) 20 chars
C) 30 chars
D) 64 chars
Correct Answer: C

39. Question: What is the MySQL command line client command used to execute an SQL script from a file?
A) EXECUTE
B) RUN
C) SOURCE
D) LOAD
Correct Answer: C

40. Question: Which clause in a `SELECT` statement is used to specify the condition for which records should be fetched?
A) FROM
B) WHERE
C) HAVING
D) GROUP BY
Correct Answer: B

41. Question: Which operator is equivalent to `!=` in SQL for checking inequality?
A) ><
B) <>
C) !!
D) =!
Correct Answer: B

42. Question: Which operator is used for equality check with multiple values in a `WHERE` clause?
A) BETWEEN
B) LIKE
C) IN
D) EXISTS
Correct Answer: C

43. Question: What happens if you use `UPDATE table SET c2=new-value;` without a `WHERE` clause?
A) The command fails due to missing condition.
B) Only the first row is updated.
C) All rows in the table are updated.
D) Only rows with NULL values are updated.
Correct Answer: C

44. Question: Which MySQL version introduced the JSON data type for flexible schema?
A) 5.5
B) 5.6
C) 5.7
D) 8.0
Correct Answer: C

45. Question: Which MySQL version introduced Common Table Expressions (CTE) and NoSQL document store?
A) 5.5
B) 5.6
C) 5.7
D) 8.0
Correct Answer: D

46. Question: What is the name of the completely open-source clone of MySQL mentioned in the reference?
A) PostgreSQL
B) MariaDB
C) Percona Server
D) SQLite
Correct Answer: B

47. Question: What is the primary function of a database/schema in a logical layout?
A) To store the operating system files
B) To act as a namespace/container for all database objects related to a project
C) To manage network connections
D) To execute business logic
Correct Answer: B

48. Question: When inserting a new row, if a column is not specified in the `INSERT` statement, what value is assigned to it by default (assuming no default value is set)?
A) 0
B) Empty string
C) NULL
D) UNDEFINED
Correct Answer: C

49. Question: What is the purpose of the `LIMIT m, n` clause in a `SELECT` statement?
A) To select the first `m` rows and then the next `n` rows.
B) To skip the first `m` rows and select the next `n` rows.
C) To select rows between row `m` and row `n`.
D) To limit the total number of columns to `n`.
Correct Answer: B

50. Question: What is the primary benefit of using RDBMS over traditional file-based systems, as related to processing?
A) Client-side processing
B) Server-side processing
C) Distributed processing
D) Parallel processing
Correct Answer: B

51. Question: Which SQL command is used to revoke a user's access privileges?
A) DENY
B) REVOKE
C) REMOVE
D) DROP USER
Correct Answer: B

52. Question: What is the main difference in storage between CHAR and VARCHAR data types?
A) CHAR uses variable storage, VARCHAR uses fixed storage.
B) CHAR uses fixed storage, VARCHAR uses variable storage.
C) CHAR is for numbers, VARCHAR is for text.
D) CHAR is for small strings, VARCHAR is for large strings.
Correct Answer: B

53. Question: Which data type is generally slower to access and not ideal for indexing?
A) CHAR
B) VARCHAR
C) TEXT
D) INT
Correct Answer: C

54. Question: Which of the following is a relational operator used in the `WHERE` clause?
A) AND
B) IS NULL
C) <=
D) IN
Correct Answer: C

55. Question: Which of the following is a logical operator used in the `WHERE` clause?
A) =
B) >
C) NOT
D) BETWEEN
Correct Answer: C

56. Question: What is the purpose of the `CASE` expression in a `SELECT` statement?
A) To define a new table structure.
B) To perform conditional logic and return a value based on that logic.
C) To group rows with the same values.
D) To enforce a foreign key constraint.
Correct Answer: B

57. Question: Which of the following is a valid way to compare two values for equality in SQL?
A) `c1 == c2`
B) `c1 = c2`
C) `c1 EQUALS c2`
D) `c1 IS c2`
Correct Answer: B

58. Question: What is the term for the temporary, more readable name given to a column or computed value in a `SELECT` statement?
A) Synonym
B) Alias
C) Variable
D) Placeholder
Correct Answer: B

59. Question: Which of the following is a Transaction Control Language (TCL) command?
A) CREATE
B) GRANT
C) ROLLBACK
D) SELECT
Correct Answer: C

60. Question: What is the primary function of the `TRUNCATE TABLE` command (which is often classified as DDL)?
A) To delete specific rows based on a condition.
B) To remove the table structure.
C) To remove all rows from a table quickly, usually without logging individual row deletions.
D) To rename the table.
Correct Answer: C

61. Question: What is the main difference between `DELETE FROM table` and `TRUNCATE TABLE table`?
A) `DELETE` is DDL, `TRUNCATE` is DML.
B) `DELETE` is faster and cannot be rolled back.
C) `TRUNCATE` is faster and resets identity columns, while `DELETE` can be conditional and is slower.
D) `DELETE` requires a `WHERE` clause, `TRUNCATE` does not.
Correct Answer: C

62. Question: Which of the following is an example of a Data Control Language (DCL) command?
A) `INSERT`
B) `ALTER`
C) `GRANT`
D) `COMMIT`
Correct Answer: C

63. Question: What is the term for the logical container that stores all database objects related to a project?
A) Table
B) Column
C) Schema/Database
D) Index
Correct Answer: C

64. Question: In RDBMS, data is organized into which three primary components?
A) Files, folders, and documents
B) Tables, rows, and columns
C) Objects, classes, and methods
D) Nodes, edges, and properties
Correct Answer: B

65. Question: Which of the following is a feature of RDBMS that is not typically found in traditional file-based systems?
A) Data storage
B) File-locking
C) Built-in relational capabilities
D) CRUD operations
Correct Answer: C

66. Question: What does ANSI standardization of SQL ensure?
A) That SQL is case-sensitive.
B) That SQL is proprietary to a single vendor.
C) That SQL is a consistent, recognized standard across different RDBMS.
D) That SQL can only be used for DDL operations.
Correct Answer: C

67. Question: What is the primary purpose of a SQL script?
A) To define a stored procedure.
B) To write multiple SQL queries into a file for backup and restore operations.
C) To connect to a database from an application.
D) To create a new user account.
Correct Answer: B

68. Question: Which operator is used to check if a value is within a specified range (inclusive)?
A) IN
B) LIKE
C) BETWEEN
D) EXISTS
Correct Answer: C

69. Question: If you want to sort a result set by column `c1` in ascending order and then by column `c2` in descending order, what is the correct `ORDER BY` clause?
A) `ORDER BY c1 DESC, c2 ASC`
B) `ORDER BY c1 ASC, c2 DESC`
C) `ORDER BY c1, c2`
D) `ORDER BY c2 DESC, c1 ASC`
Correct Answer: B

70. Question: What is the effect of using `SELECT DISTINCT c1, c2 FROM table;`?
A) It returns unique values for column `c1` only.
B) It returns unique combinations of values for both columns `c1` and `c2`.
C) It returns all rows, but only the first two columns.
D) It sorts the results by `c1` and then `c2`.
Correct Answer: B

71. Question: Which of the following is a logical operator that negates a condition?
A) AND
B) OR
C) NOT
D) XOR
Correct Answer: C

72. Question: Which operator is used to compare two values for inequality?
A) `==`
B) `!=` or `<>`
C) `IS NOT`
D) `NOT EQUAL`
Correct Answer: B

73. Question: When inserting data into a table, if you specify the column names, what happens to the columns you omit?
A) They must be explicitly set to 0.
B) They are automatically set to the default value or NULL.
C) The insertion fails.
D) They are set to the value of the first column.
Correct Answer: B

74. Question: What is the primary benefit of using the `WHERE` clause in a `SELECT` statement?
A) To increase network traffic.
B) To fetch only the required rows, reducing network traffic.
C) To define the columns to be displayed.
D) To group the results.
Correct Answer: B

75. Question: Which of the following is a correct way to use the `LIKE` operator to find names that start with 'A'?
A) `name LIKE 'A'`
B) `name LIKE 'A%'`
C) `name LIKE '%A'`
D) `name LIKE '_A%'`
Correct Answer: B

76. Question: Which of the following is a correct way to use the `LIKE` operator to find names that have 'a' as the second letter?
A) `name LIKE 'a%'`
B) `name LIKE '_a%'`
C) `name LIKE '%a_'`
D) `name LIKE 'a_a%'`
Correct Answer: B

77. Question: What is the purpose of the `RENAME` command in SQL (DDL)?
A) To change the data in a column.
B) To change the name of a database object (e.g., a table).
C) To change the name of a column's alias.
D) To change the name of a user.
Correct Answer: B

78. Question: What is the primary difference between table-locking and row-locking?
A) Table-locking is used in RDBMS, row-locking in file systems.
B) Table-locking locks the entire table, while row-locking locks only the specific row being accessed.
C) Row-locking is faster than table-locking.
D) Table-locking is only for DDL, row-locking is for DML.
Correct Answer: B

86. Question: What is the purpose of the `SAVEPOINT` command in Transaction Control Language (TCL)?

B) To define a point within a transaction to which you can later roll back.

D) To commit the transaction and start a new one.

A) It returns TRUE if the values are the same.
B) It returns FALSE.
C) It returns UNKNOWN.

88. Question: Which operator is used in MySQL to compare two values, including NULL values, for equality?
A) `IS NULL`
B) `NULL = NULL`

89. Question: What is the term for the process of writing multiple SQL queries into a `.sql` file?

92. Question: What is the primary purpose of the `GROUP BY` clause?
A) To sort the result set.

A) SUM
B) CONCAT
C) SUBSTRING
D) REPLACE

94. Question: Which of the following is a valid way to use the `CASE` expression?
A) `SELECT c1, CASE WHEN c2 > 10 THEN 'High' END FROM table;`

C) `SELECT c1 FROM table CASE WHEN c2 > 10 THEN 'High';`

97. Question: What is the primary function of a Data File in a DBMS storage structure?

--- MCQ Batch 2 (100 Questions) ---
Topic: SQL Functions, Conditional Constructs, and DML/DDL Differences

101. Question: Which SQL command is generally faster for removing all rows from a table and is classified as DDL?
A) DELETE FROM table
B) DROP TABLE
C) TRUNCATE TABLE
D) REMOVE ALL
Correct Answer: C

102. Question: What is the key difference between `DELETE FROM table` and `TRUNCATE TABLE table` regarding transaction logging?
A) DELETE is non-logged, TRUNCATE is fully logged.
B) DELETE is fully logged, TRUNCATE is minimally logged (or not logged per row).
C) Both are fully logged.
D) Neither is logged.
Correct Answer: B

103. Question: Which command removes the table structure and all its data from the database?
A) DELETE
B) TRUNCATE
C) DROP TABLE
D) ALTER TABLE
Correct Answer: C

104. Question: What is the purpose of the `DUAL` table in SQL?
A) To store temporary user data.
B) To perform arbitrary calculations and test functions without referencing a physical table.
C) To store system metadata.
D) To manage database connections.
Correct Answer: B

105. Question: In MySQL, the `DUAL` keyword is optional. What does this imply?
A) Calculations must be performed in a separate environment.
B) The database automatically assumes a single-row context for arbitrary calculations.
C) The `DUAL` table is not supported in MySQL.
D) Only DDL commands can be executed without a table reference.
Correct Answer: B

106. Question: Which category of SQL functions takes multiple rows as input and produces a single value as output?
A) Single-row functions
B) Scalar functions
C) Multi-row or Group functions
D) Control flow functions
Correct Answer: C

B) CONCAT()

D) IFNULL()
Correct Answer: C

125. Question: What is the output of `SELECT ROUND(4.567, 2) FROM DUAL;`?
A) 4.5
B) 4.56

C) It must reference all columns in the `GROUP BY` clause.
D) It must be placed after the `HAVING` clause.

D) `HAVING employee_name = 'John'`

Topic: Transactions (ACID), Locking, and DCL

301. Question: What is a database transaction defined as?
A) A single DML query executed on the database.
B) A set of DML queries executed as a single unit.
C) A DDL command that changes the database structure.
D) A SELECT query that retrieves data.
Correct Answer: B

302. Question: Which acronym represents the four key properties of a reliable database transaction?
A) CRUD
B) SQL
C) ACID
D) DBMS
Correct Answer: C

303. Question: Which ACID property ensures that all queries in a transaction are executed as a single unit, and if any query fails, all others are discarded?
A) Consistency
B) Isolation
C) Atomicity
D) Durability
Correct Answer: C

304. Question: Which ACID property ensures that when a transaction is completed, all clients see the same, correct data?
A) Consistency
B) Isolation
C) Atomicity
D) Durability
Correct Answer: A

A) Consistency
B) Isolation
C) Atomicity
D) Durability
Correct Answer: B

B) Isolation
C) Atomicity
D) Durability
Correct Answer: D

Topic: Sub-queries, Views, Indexes, Constraints, and ALTER TABLE

501. Question: What is a sub-query defined as in SQL?

B) A query that is used to define a view.

D) A query that is used to define a stored procedure.

502. Question: If no optimization is enabled, how often is a sub-query executed for a `SELECT` statement?

B) Once for each row of the outer query result.

D) Full dependency
Correct Answer: C

585. Question: Which of the following is a valid way to rename a table using the `ALTER TABLE` command?
A) `ALTER TABLE old_name RENAME TO new_name;`
B) `RENAME TABLE old_name TO new_name;`
C) `ALTER TABLE old_name RENAME new_name;`
D) Both A and B (depending on the RDBMS).
Correct Answer: D

586. Question: Which of the following is a key characteristic of a `UNIQUE` index?
A) It is always a clustered index.
B) It is automatically created when a `UNIQUE` constraint is defined.
C) It cannot be created on multiple columns.
D) It must be created manually.
Correct Answer: B

587. Question: What is the primary purpose of the `CHECK` constraint?
A) To ensure uniqueness.
B) To ensure non-null values.
C) To enforce domain integrity by limiting column values.
D) To enforce referential integrity.
Correct Answer: C

588. Question: Which of the following is a key characteristic of a `Simple View` regarding DML operations?

B) DML operations on the view affect the underlying table.
C) DML operations on the view only affect the view itself.
D) DML operations require a `CHECK OPTION`.
Correct Answer: B

589. Question: What is the term for the process of optimizing a query to reduce its execution cost?
A) Query Parsing
B) Query Compilation
C) Query Optimization
D) Query Execution
Correct Answer: C

590. Question: Which of the following is a key reason to avoid creating indexes on columns that are not used for frequent search, ordering, or grouping?

B) Indexes consume disk space.
C) Indexes must be updated during DML operations.
D) All of the above.
Correct Answer: D

591. Question: What is the term for a query that is executed for each row of the outer query result?
A) Non-correlated sub-query
B) Correlated sub-query
C) Multi-row sub-query
D) Simple sub-query

592. Question: Which of the following is a key benefit of using a `VIEW` for security?

B) It encrypts the data in the base tables.
C) It prevents SQL injection attacks.
D) It enforces the `NOT NULL` constraint.

593. Question: What is the term for a key that is a candidate key but is not chosen as the primary key?

B) Super Key
C) Alternate Key
D) Composite Key

594. Question: Which of the following is a key characteristic of a `Clustered Index`?

B) A table can have multiple clustered indexes.
C) It is always created on a non-unique column.
D) It is only used for `SELECT` operations.
Correct Answer: A

595. Question: What is the term for a key that can uniquely identify a row but may contain redundant attributes?
A) Primary Key
B) Candidate Key
C) Super Key
D) Foreign Key
Correct Answer: C

596. Question: Which of the following is a key characteristic of a `Non-Clustered Index`?

B) It stores the data rows themselves.
C) It stores the indexed column values and a pointer to the actual data row.
D) A table can only have one non-clustered index.

D) All of the above

Topic: Stored Procedures, Functions, and Triggers (PSM)

601. Question: What does PSM stand for in the context of RDBMS programming?

B) Persistent Stored Module

D) Programmatic System Management

605. Question: What is a key advantage of Stored Procedures, Functions, and Triggers being stored on the server in a compiled form?

691. Question: What is the term for the variables used to pass data into or out of a Stored Procedure?

B) Session Variables

D) Attributes

C) Both A and B
D) `CASE var IS 1 THEN 'A' ELSE 'B' END CASE;`

Topic: Data Collection Concepts, Methodologies, and Tools

--- MCQ Batch 10 (100 Questions) ---
Topic: Enterprise Data Management, Data Preparation, and Data Cleaning

901. Question: What is **Enterprise Data Management (EDM)**?
A) The process of storing all enterprise data in a single database.
B) The practice of organizing, governing, and optimizing organizational data throughout its lifecycle.
C) The process of only managing transactional data.
D) The technology used for data visualization.
Correct Answer: B

902. Question: Which of the following is a key goal of Enterprise Data Management?
A) Ensuring data accuracy and consistency.
B) Managing the data lifecycle (data lineage).
C) Ensuring compliance and reducing risk.
D) All of the above.
Correct Answer: D

903. Question: What is the term for the framework that governs how data is organized, structured, and managed across an organization?
A) Data Mining
B) Data Governance
C) Data Visualization
D) Data Entry
Correct Answer: B

904. Question: Which of the following is a key component of **Data Governance**?
A) Defining data ownership and quality standards.
B) Performing real-time transactional updates.
C) Managing user sessions.
D) Enforcing the Primary Key constraint.
Correct Answer: A

905. Question: What is **Data Lifecycle Management (DLM)**?
A) The process of only managing data in the active usage phase.
B) An approach to managing data from its creation to its eventual destruction.
C) The process of archiving data for long-term storage.
D) The process of data transformation.
Correct Answer: B

906. Question: Which of the following is a typical stage in the Data Lifecycle?
A) Creation/Capture
B) Storage/Maintenance
C) Usage/Analysis
D) All of the above
Correct Answer: D

907. Question: What is the final stage of the Data Lifecycle?
A) Usage
B) Archiving
C) Destruction/Disposal
D) Transformation
Correct Answer: C

908. Question: What is **Data Lineage**?
A) The process of cleaning data.
B) The process of tracking the origin, movement, and transformations of data throughout its lifecycle.
C) The process of defining data ownership.
D) The process of data visualization.
Correct Answer: B

909. Question: What is **Data Preparation**?
A) The process of only collecting raw data.
B) The process of cleaning and transforming raw data prior to processing and analysis.
C) The process of generating reports.
D) The process of data storage.
Correct Answer: B

910. Question: Which of the following is a key step in the Data Preparation process?
A) Gathering data
B) Cleansing and validating data
C) Transforming and enriching data
D) All of the above
Correct Answer: D

911. Question: What is **Data Cleaning** (or Data Cleansing)?
A) The process of only removing duplicate data.
B) The process of fixing or removing incorrect, corrupted, incorrectly formatted, duplicate, or incomplete data within a dataset.
C) The process of converting data to a new format.
D) The process of data visualization.
Correct Answer: B

912. Question: Which of the following is a common technique for **Data Cleaning**?
A) Removing duplicate or irrelevant observations.
B) Fixing structural errors (e.g., inconsistent capitalization).
C) Handling missing data.
D) All of the above.
Correct Answer: D

913. Question: What is the term for data that is missing a value for one or more variables?
A) Outlier
B) Irrelevant Data
C) Missing Data
D) Duplicate Data
Correct Answer: C

914. Question: Which of the following is a common method for handling **Missing Data**?
A) Deletion (removing rows or columns with missing values).
B) Imputation (filling in missing values with a calculated value like mean or median).
C) Using advanced techniques like predictive modeling.
D) All of the above.
Correct Answer: D

915. Question: What is the risk of using **Deletion** (removing rows) to handle missing data?
A) It can introduce bias if the missing data is not missing completely at random.
B) It can increase the complexity of the analysis.
C) It can make the data less accurate.
D) It can create duplicate data.
Correct Answer: A

916. Question: What is **Imputation**?
A) The process of deleting rows with missing values.
B) The process of filling in missing values with a substitute value.
C) The process of detecting outliers.
D) The process of removing duplicate data.
Correct Answer: B

917. Question: What is an **Outlier**?
A) A data point that is exactly the same as the mean.
B) A data point that significantly deviates from other observations.
C) A missing data point.
D) A duplicate data point.
Correct Answer: B

918. Question: Which of the following is a common method for handling **Outliers**?
A) Removing the rows containing the outliers.
B) Coercing the outlier to a boundary value (capping).
C) Transforming the data (e.g., using a log transformation).
D) All of the above.
Correct Answer: D

919. Question: What is the term for the process of ensuring that data values are consistent in format and representation (e.g., standardizing date formats)?
A) Data Imputation
B) Structural Error Correction
C) Outlier Detection
D) Data Enrichment
Correct Answer: B

920. Question: What is the term for the process of combining data from multiple sources to create a more complete and valuable dataset?
A) Data Cleansing
B) Data Enrichment
C) Data Imputation
D) Data Normalization
Correct Answer: B

921. Question: Which of the following is a key benefit of **Data Preparation**?
A) It ensures the data is in a format suitable for analysis.
B) It improves the accuracy and reliability of the analysis results.
C) It reduces the time spent on analysis.
D) All of the above.
Correct Answer: D

922. Question: What is the term for the process of identifying and removing records that are identical or nearly identical in a dataset?

--- MCQ Batch 11 (100 Questions) ---
Topic: Data Lake, Data Warehouse, Lakehouse, and Delta Lake

1001. Question: What is a **Data Lake**?
A) A system optimized for transactional processing.
B) A centralized repository that stores all your data, both structured and unstructured, in its native format.
C) A highly structured database for reporting.
D) A subset of a Data Warehouse focused on a single subject.
Correct Answer: B

1002. Question: What is the primary characteristic of data stored in a Data Lake?
A) It is always highly structured and cleaned.
B) It is stored in its native, raw format.
C) It is only historical data.
D) It is only transactional data.
Correct Answer: B

1003. Question: Which of the following is a key component of Data Lake architecture?
A) Storage (e.g., S3, ADLS)
B) Compute (e.g., Spark, Hadoop)
C) Both A and B
D) Only a highly normalized relational database
Correct Answer: C

1004. Question: What is the concept of **Schema-on-Read** primarily associated with?
A) Data Warehouse
B) OLTP systems
C) Data Lake
D) Data Mart
Correct Answer: C

1005. Question: What is the concept of **Schema-on-Write** primarily associated with?
A) Data Lake
B) Data Warehouse
C) NoSQL databases
D) Graph databases
Correct Answer: B

1006. Question: Which system is generally preferred for storing unstructured and semi-structured data for future use and advanced analytics?
A) Data Warehouse
B) Data Lake
C) OLTP system
D) Data Mart
Correct Answer: B

1007. Question: Which system is generally preferred for storing cleaned, structured data for business intelligence and reporting?
A) Data Lake
B) Data Warehouse
C) OLTP system
D) NoSQL database
Correct Answer: B

1008. Question: What is a key challenge often associated with Data Lakes?
A) High cost of storage.
B) Data Swamp (lack of governance leading to unusable data).
C) Difficulty in storing structured data.
D) Slow ingestion of data.
Correct Answer: B

1009. Question: What is a **Data Lakehouse**?
A) A new type of NoSQL database.
B) A data storage architecture that combines the flexibility of Data Lakes with the data management and structure of Data Warehouses.
C) A Data Warehouse that only stores unstructured data.
D) A Data Lake that only stores transactional data.
Correct Answer: B

1010. Question: Which technology is a common foundation for implementing a Data Lakehouse architecture?
A) MySQL
B) Delta Lake
C) MongoDB
D) Cassandra
Correct Answer: B

1011. Question: Which of the following is a key feature that a Data Lakehouse aims to bring from the Data Warehouse world to the Data Lake?
A) Schema enforcement and governance.
B) Storage of raw, unstructured data.
C) High-speed transactional processing.
D) Row-optimized storage.
Correct Answer: A

1012. Question: What is **Delta Lake**?
A) A proprietary database technology.
B) An open-source storage layer that brings reliability (ACID properties) to Data Lakes.
C) A new type of OLTP system.
D) A tool for data visualization.
Correct Answer: B

1013. Question: Which property does Delta Lake bring to Data Lakes, traditionally associated with relational databases?
A) High latency
B) ACID properties (Atomicity, Consistency, Isolation, Durability)
C) Schema-on-Read
D) Denormalization
Correct Answer: B

1014. Question: What is **Time Travel** in the context of Delta Lake?
A) The ability to query previous versions of the data.
B) The ability to predict future data trends.
C) The ability to store data from different time zones.
D) The ability to delete data after a certain time.
Correct Answer: A

1015. Question: Which of the following is a key benefit of using Delta Lake for analytics and AI?
A) Improved data reliability and quality.
B) Support for batch and streaming data operations.
C) Simplified data management and governance.
D) All of the above.
Correct Answer: D

1016. Question: In the context of Data Lakes, what does **ELT** (Extract, Load, Transform) refer to?
A) Data is transformed before being loaded into the Data Lake.
B) Data is loaded into the Data Lake first, then transformed within the lake.
C) Data is only extracted and loaded, with no transformation.
D) Data is only transformed, with no extraction or loading.
Correct Answer: B

1017. Question: Which data architecture typically uses **ETL** (Extract, Transform, Load) where transformation happens before loading into the final repository?
A) Data Lake
B) Data Warehouse
C) Data Lakehouse
D) NoSQL database
Correct Answer: B

1018. Question: Which of the following is a key difference in data quality between a traditional Data Lake and a Data Warehouse?
A) Data Lake data is always clean; Data Warehouse data is often raw.
B) Data Warehouse data is cleaned and structured; Data Lake data is often raw and may have quality issues.
C) Both systems only store clean data.
D) Both systems only store raw data.
Correct Answer: B

1019. Question: Which system is optimized for **data storage management** in terms of cost-effectiveness for massive amounts of raw data?
A) Data Warehouse
B) Data Lake (using object storage like S3)
C) OLTP system
D) Data Mart
Correct Answer: B

B) It only supports unstructured data.

--- MCQ Batch 12 (100 Questions) ---
Topic: Database Schema Design, Normal Forms, and ER Diagrams

1101. Question: What is a **Database Schema**?
A) The physical arrangement of data on the disk.
B) The logical and organized structure of a database, including tables, columns, relationships, and constraints.
C) The set of data stored in the database at a particular moment.
D) The software used to manage the database.
Correct Answer: B

1102. Question: Which of the following is a key step in the Database Schema Design process?
A) Determining the purpose of the database.
B) Defining the entities and their attributes.
C) Defining the relationships between entities.
D) All of the above.
Correct Answer: D

1103. Question: What is the primary goal of **Relational Database Modeling**?
A) To increase data redundancy.
B) To reduce data duplication and ensure data integrity.
C) To optimize for unstructured data storage.
D) To simplify complex queries.
Correct Answer: B

1104. Question: What does **ER Model** stand for?
A) Entity-Relationship Model
B) Enterprise Resource Model
C) External Report Model
D) Entity Retrieval Model
Correct Answer: A

1105. Question: What is the primary purpose of the **Entity-Relationship Model (ERM)**?
A) To define the physical storage structure of the database.
B) To represent the logical structure of a database conceptually.
C) To manage user access permissions.
D) To execute SQL queries.
Correct Answer: B

1106. Question: Which of the following is a main component of the ER Model?
A) Entity
B) Attribute
C) Relationship
D) All of the above
Correct Answer: D

1107. Question: In an ER Diagram, what is typically represented by a rectangle?
A) Attribute
B) Relationship
C) Entity
D) Primary Key
Correct Answer: C

1108. Question: In an ER Diagram, what is typically represented by an oval?
A) Entity
B) Relationship
C) Attribute
D) Primary Key
Correct Answer: C

1109. Question: In an ER Diagram, what is typically represented by a diamond shape?
A) Entity
B) Attribute
C) Relationship
D) Primary Key
Correct Answer: C

1110. Question: What is an **Attribute** that can be divided into smaller sub-parts (e.g., Address into Street, City, Zip)?
A) Simple Attribute
B) Composite Attribute
C) Multi-valued Attribute
D) Derived Attribute
Correct Answer: B

1111. Question: What is an **Attribute** whose value can be calculated from other attributes (e.g., Age from Date of Birth)?
A) Simple Attribute
B) Composite Attribute
C) Multi-valued Attribute
D) Derived Attribute
Correct Answer: D

1112. Question: What is an **Attribute** that can have more than one value for a single entity (e.g., Phone Numbers)?
A) Simple Attribute
B) Composite Attribute
C) Multi-valued Attribute
D) Derived Attribute
Correct Answer: C

1113. Question: What is a **Strong Entity**?
A) An entity that depends on another entity for its existence.
B) An entity that has a Primary Key of its own.
C) An entity that has no attributes.
D) An entity that is not related to any other entity.
Correct Answer: B

1114. Question: What is a **Weak Entity**?
A) An entity that has a Primary Key of its own.
B) An entity that depends on a Strong Entity (Owner Entity) for its existence and identification.
C) An entity that has no attributes.
D) An entity that is not related to any other entity.
Correct Answer: B

1115. Question: What is the term for the number of entity sets that participate in a relationship?
A) Cardinality
B) Modality
C) Degree of Relationship
D) Connectivity
Correct Answer: C

1116. Question: What is the term for the number of instances of one entity that can be associated with the instances of another entity in a relationship?
A) Degree of Relationship
B) Cardinality (or Cardinality Ratio)
C) Modality
D) Connectivity
Correct Answer: B

1117. Question: Which type of relationship is represented by "1:N" (One-to-Many)?
A) Unary
B) Binary
C) Ternary
D) Quaternary
Correct Answer: B

1118. Question: What is **Normalization** in the context of database design?
A) The process of increasing data redundancy to improve read performance.
B) The process of organizing the columns and tables of a relational database to minimize data redundancy and dependency.
C) The process of converting unstructured data to structured data.
D) The process of creating indexes for faster searching.
Correct Answer: B

1119. Question: What is the goal of achieving **First Normal Form (1NF)**?
A) Eliminating partial dependency.
B) Eliminating transitive dependency.
C) Ensuring all attributes are atomic and eliminating repeating groups.
D) Ensuring every determinant is a candidate key.
Correct Answer: C

1120. Question: A table is in **First Normal Form (1NF)** if:
A) It has a Primary Key.
B) All non-key attributes are fully dependent on the Primary Key.
C) All attributes are atomic, and there are no repeating groups.
D) There are no transitive dependencies.
Correct Answer: C

1121. Question: A table is in **Second Normal Form (2NF)** if:
A) It is in 1NF.
B) All non-key attributes are fully dependent on the Primary Key (eliminating partial dependency).
C) Both A and B.
D) There are no transitive dependencies.
Correct Answer: C

1122. Question: What is a **Partial Dependency**?
A) A non-key attribute depends on another non-key attribute.
B) A non-key attribute depends on only a part of the Composite Primary Key.
C) A non-key attribute depends on the entire Primary Key.
D) A Primary Key depends on a non-key attribute.
Correct Answer: B

1123. Question: A table is in **Third Normal Form (3NF)** if:
A) It is in 2NF.
B) There are no transitive dependencies (non-key attributes do not depend on other non-key attributes).
C) Both A and B.
D) Every determinant is a candidate key.
Correct Answer: C

1124. Question: What is a **Transitive Dependency**?
A) A non-key attribute depends on only a part of the Composite Primary Key.
B) A non-key attribute depends on another non-key attribute.
C) A non-key attribute depends on the entire Primary Key.
D) A Primary Key depends on a non-key attribute.
Correct Answer: B

1125. Question: What is **Boyce-Codd Normal Form (BCNF)**?
A) A less strict version of 3NF.
B) A stricter version of 3NF, where every determinant must be a candidate key.
C) A form that allows transitive dependencies.
D) A form that allows partial dependencies.
Correct Answer: B

1126. Question: What is a **Determinant** in the context of normalization?
A) An attribute that is determined by another attribute.
B) An attribute or set of attributes that determines the value of another attribute.
C) An attribute that is part of the Primary Key.
D) An attribute that is not part of the Primary Key.
Correct Answer: B

1127. Question: Which of the following is a key benefit of **Normalization**?
A) Faster query performance for all queries.
B) Reduced data redundancy and improved data integrity.
C) Easier storage of unstructured data.
D) Simplified data entry.
Correct Answer: B

1128. Question: What is **Denormalization**?
A) The process of moving a table to a higher Normal Form.
B) The process of intentionally introducing redundancy to improve read performance.
C) The process of converting structured data to unstructured data.
D) The process of creating an ER Diagram.
Correct Answer: B

1129. Question: Which of the following is a common reason for **Denormalization**?
A) To improve data integrity.
B) To reduce storage space.
C) To improve the performance of complex read queries (e.g., in a Data Warehouse).
D) To eliminate all data redundancy.
Correct Answer: C

1130. Question: What is the term for the process of mapping the conceptual ER Model to the logical Relational Model (tables, columns, keys)?
A) Normalization
B) Denormalization
C) Relational Mapping
D) Data Cleansing
Correct Answer: C

1131. Question: In Relational Mapping, a **Strong Entity** typically maps to:
A) A column in another table.
B) A single table in the relational schema.
C) A view.
D) A stored procedure.
Correct Answer: B

1132. Question: In Relational Mapping, a **Weak Entity** typically maps to:
A) A single table, whose Primary Key is a combination of its partial key and the Primary Key of the Owner Entity.
B) A column in the Owner Entity's table.
C) A view.
D) A stored procedure.
Correct Answer: A

1133. Question: In Relational Mapping, a **One-to-Many (1:N)** relationship typically maps to:
A) A new table.
B) A Foreign Key in the table on the "Many" side, referencing the Primary Key of the table on the "One" side.
C) A Foreign Key in the table on the "One" side.
D) A composite Primary Key in both tables.
Correct Answer: B

1134. Question: In Relational Mapping, a **Many-to-Many (M:N)** relationship typically maps to:
A) A Foreign Key in one of the tables.
B) A new, separate table (Junction Table) whose Primary Key is a composite of the Primary Keys of the two participating entities.
C) A view.
D) A stored procedure.
Correct Answer: B

1135. Question: In Relational Mapping, a **One-to-One (1:1)** relationship typically maps to:
A) A new table.
B) A Foreign Key in one of the tables, which is also a Unique Key.
C) A composite Primary Key in both tables.
D) A view.
Correct Answer: B

1136. Question: What is the term for the process of defining the constraints (e.g., Primary Key, Foreign Key, NOT NULL) in the database schema?
A) Data Cleansing
B) Data Integrity Enforcement
C) Data Transformation
D) Data Enrichment
Correct Answer: B

1137. Question: Which of the following is a key characteristic of a **Candidate Key**?
A) It can uniquely identify a row in a table.
B) It must be a single attribute.
C) It must be the Primary Key.
D) It must be a Foreign Key.
Correct Answer: A

1138. Question: What is the term for a key that is a candidate key but is not chosen as the primary key?
A) Foreign Key
B) Super Key
C) Alternate Key
D) Composite Key
Correct Answer: C

1139. Question: What is the term for a key that can uniquely identify a row but may contain redundant attributes?
A) Primary Key
B) Candidate Key
C) Super Key
D) Foreign Key
Correct Answer: C

1140. Question: Which of the following is a key characteristic of a table in **Fifth Normal Form (5NF)**?
A) It is in 4NF and cannot be decomposed into smaller tables without loss of information.
B) It is in 3NF and has no transitive dependencies.
C) It is in 2NF and has no partial dependencies.
D) It is in 1NF and has no repeating groups.
Correct Answer: A

1141. Question: What is the term for a dependency where a table cannot be decomposed into smaller tables without loss of information?
A) Functional Dependency
B) Partial Dependency
C) Join Dependency
D) Transitive Dependency
Correct Answer: C

1142. Question: Which of the following is a key characteristic of a table in **Fourth Normal Form (4NF)**?
A) It is in 3NF and has no transitive dependencies.
B) It is in 3NF and has no multi-valued dependencies.
C) It is in 2NF and has no partial dependencies.
D) It is in 1NF and has no repeating groups.
Correct Answer: B

1143. Question: What is a **Multi-valued Dependency**?
A) A non-key attribute depends on another non-key attribute.
B) An attribute that can have more than one value for a single entity.
C) A dependency where a determinant determines a set of values rather than a single value.
D) A dependency where a non-key attribute depends on only a part of the Composite Primary Key.
Correct Answer: C

1144. Question: Which of the following is a key benefit of achieving **BCNF**?
A) It eliminates all anomalies related to functional dependencies.
B) It is easier to implement than 3NF.
C) It allows for more data redundancy.
D) It is only used for unstructured data.
Correct Answer: A

--- MCQ Batch 14 (100 Questions) ---
Topic: Database Fundamentals, Storage Structures, ACID properties, and Transaction Isolation Levels

1301. Question: Which of the following is a key advantage of using a **DBMS** over a traditional **File System**?
A) Lower complexity and cost.
B) Better data security, integrity, and reduced redundancy.
C) Easier data sharing and access control.
D) Both B and C.
Correct Answer: D

1302. Question: Which of the following is a major disadvantage of using a traditional **File System** for data management?
A) High data security.
B) Difficulty in managing concurrent access.
C) Easy data sharing.
D) Built-in data integrity checks.
Correct Answer: B

1303. Question: What is **Data Redundancy**?
A) The process of storing data in a single location.
B) The duplication of data in multiple locations within a database or file system.
C) The process of ensuring data consistency.
D) The process of data backup.
Correct Answer: B

1304. Question: Which system is designed to minimize **Data Redundancy**?
A) File System
B) DBMS
C) Spreadsheet
D) Text File
Correct Answer: B

1305. Question: What is **Data Integrity**?
A) The process of ensuring data is stored in a single format.
B) The assurance that the data is accurate, consistent, and reliable.
C) The process of data encryption.
D) The process of data backup.
Correct Answer: B

1306. Question: Which system provides better mechanisms for enforcing **Data Integrity**?
A) File System
B) DBMS
C) Spreadsheet
D) Text File
Correct Answer: B

1307. Question: In a DBMS, what is the term for a logical storage unit that groups together related logical structures (like tables and views)?
A) Data File
B) Control File
C) Tablespace
D) Segment
Correct Answer: C

1308. Question: Which of the following is a key characteristic of a **Tablespace**?
A) It is a physical file on the disk.
B) It is a logical structure that maps to one or more physical data files.
C) It stores the metadata of the database.
D) It is only used for temporary data.
Correct Answer: B

1309. Question: What is a **Data File** in the context of database storage structures?
A) A logical structure that groups tables.
B) A physical operating system file that stores the actual data of the database.
C) A file that stores the database metadata.
D) A file that stores the transaction logs.
Correct Answer: B

1310. Question: What is the relationship between a **Tablespace** and a **Data File**?
A) One Data File can belong to multiple Tablespaces.
B) One Tablespace can map to multiple Data Files, but a Data File belongs to only one Tablespace.
C) They are the same thing.
D) They are completely independent.
Correct Answer: B

1311. Question: What is a **Control File** in a DBMS?
A) A file that stores the actual user data.
B) A small, critical file that contains metadata about the database's physical structure (e.g., database name, location of data files).
C) A file that stores the transaction logs.
D) A file that stores the SQL queries.
Correct Answer: B

1312. Question: Which of the following is a key characteristic of a **Control File**?
A) It is only used during normal database operation.
B) It is essential for starting and recovering the database.
C) It is a large file that stores all the data.
D) It is automatically created and managed by the user.
Correct Answer: B

1313. Question: What does the acronym **ACID** stand for in the context of database transactions?
A) Access, Consistency, Isolation, Durability
B) Atomicity, Concurrency, Integrity, Durability
C) Atomicity, Consistency, Isolation, Durability
D) Access, Concurrency, Integrity, Dependency
Correct Answer: C

1314. Question: Which **ACID** property ensures that a transaction is treated as a single, indivisible unit of work, either all of it is executed or none of it is?
A) Atomicity
B) Consistency
C) Isolation
D) Durability
Correct Answer: A

1315. Question: Which **ACID** property ensures that a transaction brings the database from one valid state to another, maintaining all defined rules and constraints?
A) Atomicity
B) Consistency
C) Isolation
D) Durability
Correct Answer: B

1316. Question: Which **ACID** property ensures that concurrent execution of transactions leaves the database in the same state that would have been obtained if the transactions were executed sequentially?
A) Atomicity
B) Consistency
C) Isolation
D) Durability
Correct Answer: C

1317. Question: Which **ACID** property ensures that once a transaction has been committed, it will remain permanent, even in the event of system failure (e.g., power loss)?
A) Atomicity
B) Consistency
C) Isolation
D) Durability
Correct Answer: D

1318. Question: What is a **Transaction Isolation Level**?
A) A measure of how many transactions can run concurrently.
B) A setting that defines the degree to which one transaction must be isolated from the data modifications made by other concurrent transactions.
C) A property that ensures data is always consistent.
D) A property that ensures data is always durable.
Correct Answer: B

1319. Question: Which of the following is the lowest **Transaction Isolation Level**?
A) Read Committed
B) Repeatable Read
C) Read Uncommitted
D) Serializable
Correct Answer: C

1320. Question: Which **Isolation Level** allows a transaction to read data that has been modified by another transaction but not yet committed (Dirty Read)?
A) Read Committed
B) Repeatable Read
C) Read Uncommitted
D) Serializable
Correct Answer: C

1321. Question: Which **Isolation Level** prevents **Dirty Reads** but allows **Non-Repeatable Reads**?
A) Read Uncommitted
B) Read Committed
C) Repeatable Read
D) Serializable
Correct Answer: B

1322. Question: What is a **Dirty Read**?
A) A transaction reads data that has been committed by another transaction.
B) A transaction reads data that has been modified by another transaction but not yet committed.
C) A transaction reads the same data twice and gets different values.
D) A transaction reads a set of rows twice and finds a new row in the second read.
Correct Answer: B

1323. Question: What is a **Non-Repeatable Read**?
A) A transaction reads data that has been modified by another transaction but not yet committed.
B) A transaction reads the same row twice and gets different values because another committed transaction modified the row between the reads.
C) A transaction reads a set of rows twice and finds a new row in the second read.
D) A transaction reads data that is not supposed to be read.
Correct Answer: B

1324. Question: Which **Isolation Level** prevents **Dirty Reads** and **Non-Repeatable Reads** but allows **Phantom Reads**?
A) Read Uncommitted
B) Read Committed
C) Repeatable Read
D) Serializable
Correct Answer: C

1325. Question: What is a **Phantom Read**?
A) A transaction reads data that has been modified by another transaction but not yet committed.
B) A transaction reads the same row twice and gets different values.
C) A transaction executes a query twice and finds a new row (a "phantom") in the second result set because another committed transaction inserted a new row.
D) A transaction reads data that is not supposed to be read.
Correct Answer: C

1326. Question: Which **Isolation Level** prevents **Dirty Reads**, **Non-Repeatable Reads**, and **Phantom Reads**?
A) Read Uncommitted
B) Read Committed
C) Repeatable Read
D) Serializable
Correct Answer: D

1327. Question: Which of the following is a key trade-off when moving to a higher **Transaction Isolation Level**?
A) Increased data consistency but decreased concurrency and performance.
B) Decreased data consistency but increased concurrency and performance.
C) Increased data redundancy.
D) Decreased data security.
Correct Answer: A

1328. Question: What is the term for the process of managing the concurrent execution of multiple transactions to ensure data integrity?
A) Data Cleansing
B) Concurrency Control
C) Data Modeling
D) Data Visualization
Correct Answer: B

1329. Question: Which of the following is a common technique for **Concurrency Control**?
A) Normalization
B) Locking (e.g., shared and exclusive locks)
C) Denormalization
D) Data Archiving
Correct Answer: B

1330. Question: What is a **Shared Lock**?
A) A lock that prevents all other transactions from accessing the data.
B) A lock that allows multiple transactions to read the data concurrently but prevents any transaction from writing to it.
C) A lock that allows only one transaction to read the data.
D) A lock that allows multiple transactions to write to the data concurrently.
Correct Answer: B

1331. Question: What is an **Exclusive Lock**?
A) A lock that allows multiple transactions to read the data concurrently.
B) A lock that allows multiple transactions to write to the data concurrently.
C) A lock that prevents all other transactions from accessing the data (reading or writing).
D) A lock that only prevents reading the data.
Correct Answer: C

1332. Question: What is a **Deadlock** in the context of transactions?
A) A situation where a transaction is waiting for a lock that will never be released.
B) A situation where two or more transactions are waiting for each other to release a lock, resulting in a standstill.
C) A situation where a transaction is rolled back.
D) A situation where a transaction is committed.
Correct Answer: B

1333. Question: Which of the following is a common technique for **Deadlock Prevention** or **Deadlock Detection and Resolution**?
A) Using a timeout mechanism.
B) Using a wait-for graph.
C) Using a strict ordering of resource requests.
D) All of the above.
Correct Answer: D

1334. Question: What is the term for the process of recording all changes made to the database in a sequential file?
A) Data File
B) Control File
C) Transaction Log (or Redo Log)
D) Tablespace
Correct Answer: C

1335. Question: Which of the following is a key function of the **Transaction Log**?
A) To store the actual user data.
B) To ensure the **Durability** property of ACID.
C) To store the database schema.
D) To manage user access.
Correct Answer: B

1336. Question: What is the term for the process of restoring the database to a consistent state after a system failure, using the transaction log?
A) Data Cleansing
B) Database Recovery
C) Data Modeling
D) Data Visualization

Topic: Advanced SQL (DDL, DML, DCL, Stored Procedures, Functions, Triggers, Conditional Constructs)

1401. Question: Which SQL command is used to add a new column to an existing table?
A) `INSERT COLUMN`
B) `UPDATE TABLE`
C) `ALTER TABLE`
D) `CREATE COLUMN`
Correct Answer: C

1402. Question: Which category of SQL commands is primarily concerned with the definition of the database structure?
A) DML
B) DCL
C) DDL
D) TCL
Correct Answer: C

1403. Question: Which SQL command is used to remove all rows from a table, but keep the table structure?
A) `DELETE FROM`
B) `DROP TABLE`
C) `TRUNCATE TABLE`
D) `REMOVE ROWS`
Correct Answer: C

1404. Question: Which SQL command is used to remove a table completely from the database?
A) `DELETE TABLE`
B) `TRUNCATE TABLE`
C) `DROP TABLE`
D) `REMOVE TABLE`
Correct Answer: C

1405. Question: Which SQL command is used to modify existing records in a table?
A) `INSERT INTO`
B) `UPDATE`
C) `ALTER TABLE`
D) `MODIFY`
Correct Answer: B

1406. Question: Which SQL command is used to retrieve data from a database?
A) `INSERT`
B) `UPDATE`
C) `SELECT`
D) `MERGE`
Correct Answer: C

1407. Question: Which category of SQL commands is used to control access to data and database objects?
A) DML
B) DCL
C) DDL
D) TCL
Correct Answer: B

1408. Question: Which SQL command is used to grant permissions to a user?
A) `GRANT`
B) `REVOKE`
C) `ALLOW`
D) `PERMIT`
Correct Answer: A

1409. Question: Which SQL command is used to remove permissions from a user?
A) `GRANT`
B) `REVOKE`
C) `DENY`
D) `REMOVE`
Correct Answer: B

1410. Question: Which category of SQL commands is used to manage transactions in the database?
A) DML
B) DCL
C) DDL
D) TCL
Correct Answer: D

1411. Question: Which TCL command is used to make all changes permanent?
A) `SAVEPOINT`
B) `ROLLBACK`
C) `COMMIT`
D) `PERSIST`
Correct Answer: C

1412. Question: Which TCL command is used to undo all changes since the last `COMMIT` or `ROLLBACK`?
A) `SAVEPOINT`
B) `ROLLBACK`
C) `COMMIT`
D) `UNDO`
Correct Answer: B

1413. Question: What is a **Stored Procedure** in SQL?
A) A SQL query that is executed only once.
B) A precompiled set of one or more SQL statements stored in the database.
C) A function that returns a single value.
D) A temporary table.
Correct Answer: B

1414. Question: What is a key advantage of using **Stored Procedures**?
A) Reduced security.
B) Improved performance due to pre-compilation and reduced network traffic.
C) Increased data redundancy.
D) They can only be used for simple `SELECT` statements.
Correct Answer: B

1415. Question: What is a **Stored Function** in SQL?
A) A precompiled set of SQL statements that can perform DML operations.
B) A routine that must return a single value and can be used within SQL expressions.
C) A routine that cannot accept input parameters.
D) A routine that is automatically executed when a DML operation occurs.
Correct Answer: B

1416. Question: What is the main difference between a **Stored Procedure** and a **Stored Function**?
A) Procedures must return a value; Functions do not.
B) Procedures can perform DML operations; Functions must return a value and are generally restricted from DML.
C) Procedures cannot accept parameters; Functions can.
D) Procedures are precompiled; Functions are not.
Correct Answer: B

1417. Question: What is a **Trigger** in SQL?
A) A manually executed stored procedure.
B) A special type of stored procedure that automatically executes when a specific event (e.g., `INSERT`, `UPDATE`, `DELETE`) occurs on a table.
C) A conditional construct used in a `WHERE` clause.
D) A function that returns a boolean value.
Correct Answer: B

1418. Question: Which of the following is a common use case for a **Trigger**?

B) Performing a simple `SELECT` query.
C) Creating a new table structure.
D) Granting user permissions.
Correct Answer: A

Topic: Data Collection, Methodologies, Tools, Data Preparation, and Data Cleaning

1601. Question: What is **Data Collection**?
A) The process of storing data in a database.
B) The process of gathering, measuring, and analyzing accurate data from various sources.
C) The process of converting data into information.
D) The process of deleting old data.
Correct Answer: B

A) Secondary Data
B) Primary Data
C) Tertiary Data
D) Internal Data
Correct Answer: B

A) Primary Data
B) Secondary Data
C) Tertiary Data
D) External Data

D) A duplicate record.

Topic: OLTP/OLAP, Data Warehousing, and Advanced Data Lake/Workflow Orchestration

1801. Question: What does **OLTP** stand for?
A) Online Logical Transaction Processing
B) Online Transaction Processing
C) Offline Transaction Planning
D) Online Analytical Processing
Correct Answer: B

1802. Question: What is the primary characteristic of an **OLTP** system?
A) High volume of complex queries.
B) High volume of short, atomic transactions (INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE).
C) Used for historical data analysis.
D) Optimized for read operations.
Correct Answer: B

1803. Question: What does **OLAP** stand for?
A) Online Logical Analysis Processing
B) Online Transaction Processing
C) Offline Analytical Planning
D) Online Analytical Processing
Correct Answer: D

1804. Question: What is the primary characteristic of an **OLAP** system?
A) High volume of short, atomic transactions.
B) Optimized for complex, read-heavy queries and historical data analysis.
C) Used for day-to-day business operations.
D) Highly normalized data structure.
Correct Answer: B

1805. Question: Which data model is typically used in **OLTP** systems?
A) Denormalized, dimensional model.
B) Highly normalized, Entity-Relationship model.
C) Key-Value store.
D) Graph model.
Correct Answer: B

1806. Question: Which data model is typically used in **OLAP** systems (Data Warehouses)?
A) Highly normalized, Entity-Relationship model.
B) Denormalized, dimensional model (Star or Snowflake Schema).
C) Document model.
D) Hierarchical model.
Correct Answer: B

1807. Question: What is a **Fact Table** in a dimensional model?
A) A table containing descriptive attributes (e.g., product name, customer address).
B) A table containing the business metrics or measures (e.g., sales amount, quantity sold).
C) A table used for security and access control.
D) A table that stores metadata.
Correct Answer: B

1808. Question: What is a **Dimension Table** in a dimensional model?
A) A table containing the business metrics or measures.
B) A table containing descriptive attributes that provide context to the facts.
C) A table that stores transaction logs.
D) A table that stores only primary keys.
Correct Answer: B

1809. Question: What is the primary difference between a **Star Schema** and a **Snowflake Schema**?
A) Star Schema uses denormalized dimensions; Snowflake Schema uses normalized dimensions.
B) Star Schema uses normalized dimensions; Snowflake Schema uses denormalized dimensions.
C) Star Schema has multiple fact tables; Snowflake Schema has only one.
D) Star Schema is used for OLTP; Snowflake Schema is used for OLAP.
Correct Answer: A

1810. Question: Which operation in OLAP involves reducing the dimensionality of the data cube by aggregating data along one or more dimensions?
A) Slice
B) Dice
C) Roll-up
D) Drill-down
Correct Answer: C

1811. Question: Which operation in OLAP involves navigating from a less detailed level to a more detailed level of data?
A) Roll-up
B) Drill-down
C) Pivot
D) Slice
Correct Answer: B

1812. Question: What is **Data Warehousing**?

C) A system for storing unstructured data.
D) A system for real-time transaction processing.
Correct Answer: B

D) Data Mining

1814. Question: Which of the following is a key characteristic of **Data Storage Management** in a cloud environment?
